      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Thimphu#Geography_and_climate" title="Thimphu">Thimphu §&nbsp;Geography and climate</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan's climate varies with elevation, from subtropical in the south to <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a> in the highlands and <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">polar-type</a> climate with year-round snow in the north. Bhutan experiences five distinct seasons: summer, <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>, autumn, winter and spring. Western Bhutan has the heavier monsoon rains; southern Bhutan has hot humid summers and cool winters; central and eastern Bhutan are temperate and drier than the west with warm summers and cool winters. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Bhutan" title="List of mammals of Bhutan">List of mammals of Bhutan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Bhutan" title="Wildlife of Bhutan">Wildlife of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Takin,_Thimphu_mini-zoo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Takin%2C_Thimphu_mini-zoo.jpg/220px-Takin%2C_Thimphu_mini-zoo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Takin%2C_Thimphu_mini-zoo.jpg/330px-Takin%2C_Thimphu_mini-zoo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Takin%2C_Thimphu_mini-zoo.jpg/440px-Takin%2C_Thimphu_mini-zoo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Takin,_Thimphu_mini-zoo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Takin" title="Takin">takin</a> is Bhutan's <a href="/wiki/National_animal" class="mw-redirect" title="National animal">national animal</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan signed the Rio <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> on 11 June 1992, and became a party to the convention on 25 August 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> It has subsequently produced a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_Action_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Biodiversity Action Plan">National Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan</a>, with two revisions, the most recent of which was received by the convention on 4 February 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-nbsap3_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbsap3-66">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Animals">Animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Animals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Himalayan_Marmot_at_Tshophu_Lake_Bhutan_091007_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Himalayan_Marmot_at_Tshophu_Lake_Bhutan_091007_b.jpg/220px-Himalayan_Marmot_at_Tshophu_Lake_Bhutan_091007_b.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Himalayan_Marmot_at_Tshophu_Lake_Bhutan_091007_b.jpg/330px-Himalayan_Marmot_at_Tshophu_Lake_Bhutan_091007_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Himalayan_Marmot_at_Tshophu_Lake_Bhutan_091007_b.jpg/440px-Himalayan_Marmot_at_Tshophu_Lake_Bhutan_091007_b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Himalayan_Marmot_at_Tshophu_Lake_Bhutan_091007_b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Himalayan Marmot at Tshophu Lake, Bhutan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan has a rich primate life, with rare species such as the <a href="/wiki/Golden_langur" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden langur">golden langur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> A variant Assamese macaque has also been recorded, which is regarded by some authorities as a new species, <i>Macaca munzala</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Bengal_tiger" title="Bengal tiger">Bengal tiger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clouded_leopard" title="Clouded leopard">clouded leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispid_hare" title="Hispid hare">hispid hare</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sloth_bear" title="Sloth bear">sloth bear</a> live in the tropical lowland and hardwood forests in the south. In the temperate zone, <a href="/wiki/Grey_langur" class="mw-redirect" title="Grey langur">grey langur</a>, tiger, <a href="/wiki/Goral" title="Goral">goral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serow" title="Serow">serow</a> are found in mixed conifer, broadleaf and pine forests. Fruit-bearing trees and bamboo provide habitat for the <a href="/wiki/Himalayan_black_bear" title="Himalayan black bear">Himalayan black bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_panda" title="Red panda">red panda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squirrel" title="Squirrel">squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sambar_(deer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sambar (deer)">sambar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sus_(genus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sus (genus)">wild pig</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barking_deer" class="mw-redirect" title="Barking deer">barking deer</a>. The alpine habitats of the great Himalayan range in the north are home to the <a href="/wiki/Snow_leopard" title="Snow leopard">snow leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_sheep" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue sheep">blue sheep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marmot" title="Marmot">marmot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_wolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Tibetan wolf">Tibetan wolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Himalayan_musk_deer" class="mw-redirect" title="Himalayan musk deer">Himalayan musk deer</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Takin" title="Takin">takin</a>, Bhutan's <a href="/wiki/National_animal" class="mw-redirect" title="National animal">national animal</a>. The endangered wild water buffalo occurs in southern Bhutan, although in small numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>More than 770 species of bird have been recorded in Bhutan. The globally endangered <a href="/wiki/White-winged_duck" title="White-winged duck">white-winged duck</a> has been added recently in 2006 to Bhutan's bird list.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Plants">Plants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Plants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>More than 5,400 species of plants are found in Bhutan,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> including <i><a href="/wiki/Pedicularis_cacuminidenta" title="Pedicularis cacuminidenta">Pedicularis cacuminidenta</a></i>. Fungi form a key part of Bhutanese ecosystems, with <a href="/wiki/Mycorrhizal" class="mw-redirect" title="Mycorrhizal">mycorrhizal</a> species providing forest trees with mineral nutrients necessary for growth, and with wood decay and litter decomposing species playing an important role in natural recycling. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation">Conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Bhutan" title="List of protected areas of Bhutan">List of protected areas of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="noresize thumb tleft" style=";"> 
       <div class="thumbinner" style="overflow:hidden;width:292px;"> 
        <div class="thumbimage" style="overflow:hidden; position:relative; background-color:white;"> 
         <div style=";left:0px; top:0px; width:300px; position:absolute;"> 
          <div class="noresize">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png" title="File:Bhutan protected areas location map.png"><img alt="Bhutan protected areas location map.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png/300px-Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="196" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png/450px-Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png/600px-Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="653"></a>
          </div>
         </div> 
         <div style="text-align:left; background-color:transparent; line-height:110%;"> 
          <div id="annotation_63x57" style="position:absolute; left:63px; top:57px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Jigme_Dorji_National_Park" title="Jigme Dorji National Park">JDNP</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_75x80" style="position:absolute; left:75px; top:80px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><i><a href="/wiki/Motithang_Takin_Preserve" title="Motithang Takin Preserve">Motithang</a></i></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_116x50" style="position:absolute; left:116px; top:50px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Wangchuck_Centennial_National_Park" title="Wangchuck Centennial National Park">WCNP</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_220x65" style="position:absolute; left:220px; top:65px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Bumdeling_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Bumdeling Wildlife Sanctuary">BWS</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_150x90" style="position:absolute; left:150px; top:90px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Phrumsengla_National_Park" title="Phrumsengla National Park">PNP</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_264x138" style="position:absolute; left:264px; top:138px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Jomotsangkha_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Jomotsangkha Wildlife Sanctuary">JWS</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_20x100" style="position:absolute; left:20px; top:100px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Jigme_Khesar_Strict_Nature_Reserve" title="Jigme Khesar Strict Nature Reserve">JKSNR</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_115x110" style="position:absolute; left:115px; top:110px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Jigme_Singye_Wangchuck_National_Park" title="Jigme Singye Wangchuck National Park">JSWNP</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_75x145" style="position:absolute; left:75px; top:145px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Phibsoo_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Phibsoo Wildlife Sanctuary">PWS</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_150x140" style="position:absolute; left:150px; top:140px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Royal_Manas_National_Park" title="Royal Manas National Park">RMNP</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_250x100" style="position:absolute; left:250px; top:100px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Sakteng_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Sakteng Wildlife Sanctuary">SWS</a></small></span>
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div style="visibility:hidden">
          <div class="noresize">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png" title="File:Bhutan protected areas location map.png"><img alt="Bhutan protected areas location map.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png/300px-Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="196" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png/450px-Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png/600px-Bhutan_protected_areas_location_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="653"></a>
          </div>
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Bhutan" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected areas of Bhutan">Protected areas of Bhutan</a> in lavender; <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_corridor" title="Wildlife corridor">biological corridors</a> in green.
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Eastern <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> have been identified as a global <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> hotspot and counted among the 234 globally outstanding <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a> of the world in a comprehensive analysis of global biodiversity undertaken by <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a> between 1995 and 1997. </p>
      <p>According to the Swiss-based <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a>, Bhutan is viewed as a model for proactive <a href="/wiki/Conservation_movement" title="Conservation movement">conservation</a> initiatives. The Kingdom has received international acclaim for its commitment to the maintenance of its biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN-1/2012_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-1/2012-73">[73]</a></sup> This is reflected in the decision to maintain at least sixty percent of the land area under <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forest</a> cover, to designate more than 40%<sup id="cite_ref-BTF1_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTF1-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BTF2_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTF2-75">[75]</a></sup> of its territory as national parks, reserves and other protected areas, and most recently to identify a further nine percent of land area as biodiversity corridors linking the protected areas. All of Bhutan's protected land is connected to one another through a vast network of biological corridors, allowing animals to migrate freely throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-76">[76]</a></sup> Environmental conservation has been placed at the core of the nation's development strategy, the middle path. It is not treated as a sector but rather as a set of concerns that must be mainstreamed in Bhutan's overall approach to development planning and to be buttressed by the force of law. The country's constitution mentions environment standards in multiple sections.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Bhutan" title="Environmental issues in Bhutan">Environmental issues in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Asian_Black_Bear_Ursus_thibetanus_by_Dr._Raju_Kasambe_04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Asian_Black_Bear_Ursus_thibetanus_by_Dr._Raju_Kasambe_04.jpg/220px-Asian_Black_Bear_Ursus_thibetanus_by_Dr._Raju_Kasambe_04.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Asian_Black_Bear_Ursus_thibetanus_by_Dr._Raju_Kasambe_04.jpg/330px-Asian_Black_Bear_Ursus_thibetanus_by_Dr._Raju_Kasambe_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Asian_Black_Bear_Ursus_thibetanus_by_Dr._Raju_Kasambe_04.jpg/440px-Asian_Black_Bear_Ursus_thibetanus_by_Dr._Raju_Kasambe_04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Asian_Black_Bear_Ursus_thibetanus_by_Dr._Raju_Kasambe_04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Himalayan_black_bear" title="Himalayan black bear">Himalayan black bear</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although Bhutan's natural heritage is still largely intact, the government has said that it cannot be taken for granted and that conservation of the natural environment must be considered one of the challenges that will need to be addressed in the years ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Nearly 56.3% of all Bhutanese are involved with agriculture, forestry or conservation.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-77">[77]</a></sup> The government aims to promote conservation as part of its plan to target Gross National Happiness. It currently has net negative<sup id="cite_ref-:1_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-76">[76]</a></sup> greenhouse gas emissions because the small amount of pollution it creates is absorbed by the forests that cover most of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-79">[79]</a></sup> While the entire country collectively produces 2,200,000 metric tons (2,200,000 long tons; 2,400,000 short tons) of carbon dioxide a year, the immense forest covering 72% of the country acts as a carbon sink, absorbing more than four million tons of carbon dioxide every year.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-76">[76]</a></sup> Bhutan had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 8.85/10, ranking it 16th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-80">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan has a number of progressive environmental policies that have caused the head of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">UNFCCC</a> to call it an "inspiration and role model for the world on how economies and different countries can address climate change while at the same time improving the life of the citizen."<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> For example, electric cars have been pushed in the country and as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> make up a tenth of all cars. Because the country gets most of its energy from <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric power</a>, it does not emit significant greenhouse gases for energy production.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Pressures on the natural environment, fueled by a complex array of forces, are already evident. They include: population pressures, agricultural modernization, poaching, hydro-power development, mineral extraction, industrialization, urbanization, sewage and waste disposal, tourism, competition for available land, road construction and the provision of other physical infrastructure associated with social and economic development.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In practice, the overlap of these extensive protected lands with populated areas has led to mutual habitat encroachment. Protected wildlife has entered agricultural areas, trampling crops and killing livestock. In response, Bhutan has implemented an insurance scheme, begun constructing solar powered alarm fences, watch towers, and search lights, and has provided fodder and salt licks outside human settlement areas to encourage animals to stay away.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The huge market value of the <i><a href="/wiki/Ophiocordyceps_sinensis" title="Ophiocordyceps sinensis">Ophiocordyceps sinensis</a></i> fungus crop collected from the wild has also resulted in unsustainable exploitation which is proving very difficult to regulate.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan has enforced a plastic ban rule from 1 April 2019, where plastic bags were replaced by alternative bags made of jute and other biodegradable material.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bhutan" title="Politics of Bhutan">Politics of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BhutanroyalvisitNovember_21,_2011_-4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/BhutanroyalvisitNovember_21%2C_2011_-4.jpg/220px-BhutanroyalvisitNovember_21%2C_2011_-4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/34/BhutanroyalvisitNovember_21%2C_2011_-4.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="252" data-file-height="180"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BhutanroyalvisitNovember_21,_2011_-4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/King_of_Bhutan" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Bhutan">King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jetsun_Pema" title="Jetsun Pema">Queen</a> of Bhutan with the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Japan" title="Emperor of Japan">Emperor of Japan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary">parliamentary</a> form of government. The reigning monarch is <a href="/wiki/Jigme_Khesar_Namgyel_Wangchuck" title="Jigme Khesar Namgyel Wangchuck">Jigme Khesar Namgyel Wangchuck</a>. The current <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bhutan" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Bhutan">Prime Minister of Bhutan</a> is <a href="/wiki/Lotay_Tshering" title="Lotay Tshering">Lotay Tshering</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Druk_Nyamrup_Tshogpa" title="Druk Nyamrup Tshogpa">Druk Nyamrup Tshogpa</a> Party. Bhutan's democratic transition in 2008 is seen as an evolution of its social contract with the monarchy since 1907.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-86">[86]</a></sup> In 2019, Bhutan was classified in the <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_regime" title="Hybrid regime">hybrid regime</a> alongside regional neighbors Nepal and Bangladesh. Minorities are increasingly represented in Bhutan's government since 2008, including in the cabinet, parliament and local government.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Druk_Gyalpo" title="Druk Gyalpo">Druk Gyalpo</a></i> (<i>Dragon King</i>) is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The political system grants <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a>. It consists of the <a href="/wiki/National_Council_(Bhutan)" title="National Council (Bhutan)">National Council</a>, an upper house with 25 elected members; and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Bhutan)" title="National Assembly (Bhutan)">National Assembly</a> with 47 elected lawmakers from <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Bhutan" title="List of political parties in Bhutan">political parties</a>. </p>
      <p>Executive power is exercised by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_(Bhutan)" title="Council of Ministers (Bhutan)">Council of Ministers</a> led by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bhutan" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Bhutan">Prime Minister</a>. Legislative power is vested in both the government and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Bhutan)" title="National Assembly (Bhutan)">National Assembly</a>. Judicial power is vested in the courts. The legal system originates from the semi-theocratic <a href="/wiki/Tsa_Yig" title="Tsa Yig">Tsa Yig</a> code, and was influenced by <a href="/wiki/English_common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="English common law">English common law</a> during the 20th century. The <a href="/wiki/Chief_justice" title="Chief justice">chief justice</a> is the administrative head of the judiciary. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The first <a href="/wiki/2008_Bhutanese_general_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Bhutanese general election">general elections</a> for the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Bhutan)" title="National Assembly (Bhutan)">National Assembly</a> were held on 24 March 2008. The chief contestants were the <a href="/wiki/Bhutan_Peace_and_Prosperity_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhutan Peace and Prosperity Party">Bhutan Peace and Prosperity Party</a> (DPT) led by <a href="/wiki/Jigme_Thinley" title="Jigme Thinley">Jigme Thinley</a> and the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Party_(Bhutan)" title="People's Democratic Party (Bhutan)">People's Democratic Party</a> (PDP) led by <a href="/wiki/Sangay_Ngedup" title="Sangay Ngedup">Sangay Ngedup</a>. The DPT won the elections, taking 45 out of 47 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jigme_Thinley" title="Jigme Thinley">Jigme Thinley</a> served as Prime Minister from 2008 to 2013. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Party_(Bhutan)" title="People's Democratic Party (Bhutan)">People's Democratic Party</a> came to power in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Bhutanese_National_Assembly_election" title="2013 Bhutanese National Assembly election">2013 elections</a>. It won 32 seats and 54.88% of the vote. PDP leader <a href="/wiki/Tshering_Tobgay" title="Tshering Tobgay">Tshering Tobgay</a> served as Prime Minister from 2013 to 2018. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Druk_Nyamrup_Tshogpa" title="Druk Nyamrup Tshogpa">Druk Nyamrup Tshogpa</a> won the largest number of seats in the <a href="/wiki/2018_Bhutanese_National_Assembly_election" title="2018 Bhutanese National Assembly election">2018 National Assembly Election</a>, bringing <a href="/wiki/Lotay_Tshering" title="Lotay Tshering">Lotay Tshering</a> to premiership and <a href="/wiki/Druk_Nyamrup_Tshogpa" title="Druk Nyamrup Tshogpa">Druk Nyamrup Tshogpa</a> into the government for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bhutan" title="Foreign relations of Bhutan">Foreign relations of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_Mission_in_New_York.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Bhutan_Mission_in_New_York.jpg/170px-Bhutan_Mission_in_New_York.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Bhutan_Mission_in_New_York.jpg/255px-Bhutan_Mission_in_New_York.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Bhutan_Mission_in_New_York.jpg/340px-Bhutan_Mission_in_New_York.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_Mission_in_New_York.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The permanent mission of Bhutan to the United Nations in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_shakes_hands_with_Bhutanese_Prime_Minister_Tobgay_before_bilateral_meeting_at_Vibrant.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Secretary_Kerry_shakes_hands_with_Bhutanese_Prime_Minister_Tobgay_before_bilateral_meeting_at_Vibrant.jpg/260px-Secretary_Kerry_shakes_hands_with_Bhutanese_Prime_Minister_Tobgay_before_bilateral_meeting_at_Vibrant.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Secretary_Kerry_shakes_hands_with_Bhutanese_Prime_Minister_Tobgay_before_bilateral_meeting_at_Vibrant.jpg/390px-Secretary_Kerry_shakes_hands_with_Bhutanese_Prime_Minister_Tobgay_before_bilateral_meeting_at_Vibrant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Secretary_Kerry_shakes_hands_with_Bhutanese_Prime_Minister_Tobgay_before_bilateral_meeting_at_Vibrant.jpg/520px-Secretary_Kerry_shakes_hands_with_Bhutanese_Prime_Minister_Tobgay_before_bilateral_meeting_at_Vibrant.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2951" data-file-height="1962"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_shakes_hands_with_Bhutanese_Prime_Minister_Tobgay_before_bilateral_meeting_at_Vibrant.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bhutan" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Bhutan">Prime Minister of Bhutan</a> <a href="/wiki/Tshering_Tobgay" title="Tshering Tobgay">Tshering Tobgay</a> with <a href="/wiki/U.S._Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Secretary of State">U.S. Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the early 20th century, Bhutan became a <i>de facto</i> protectorate of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Punakha" title="Treaty of Punakha">Treaty of Punakha</a> in 1910. British protection guarded Bhutan from an <a href="/wiki/Tibet_(1912-1951)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tibet (1912-1951)">independent Tibet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qing_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing China">Qing China</a>. In the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Revolution" title="Chinese Communist Revolution">Chinese Communist Revolution</a>, Bhutan signed a friendship treaty with the newly independent <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_India" title="Dominion of India">Dominion of India</a> in 1949. Its concerns were exacerbated after the <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_of_Tibet_into_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Incorporation of Tibet into the People's Republic of China">Chinese incorporation of Tibet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bhutanstudies.org.bt_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bhutanstudies.org.bt-91">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Relations with <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> remained strained due to <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_refugees" title="Bhutanese refugees">Bhutanese refugees</a>. Bhutan joined the United Nations in 1971. It was the second country to recognize Bangladesh's <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_Bangladesh" title="Provisional Government of Bangladesh">independence</a> in 1971. It became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation</a> (<a href="/wiki/SAARC" class="mw-redirect" title="SAARC">SAARC</a>) in 1985.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The country is a member of 150 international organizations,<sup id="cite_ref-bhutanstudies.org.bt_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bhutanstudies.org.bt-91">[91]</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal_Initiative" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay of Bengal Initiative">Bay of Bengal Initiative</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBIN" class="mw-redirect" title="BBIN">BBIN</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a>. </p>
      <p>Bhutan maintains strong economic, strategic, and military relations with India.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> In February 2007, the Indo-Bhutan Friendship Treaty was substantially revised, clarifying Bhutan's full control of its foreign relations, as well as its independence and sovereignty. Whereas the Treaty of 1949, Article 2 stated: "The Government of India undertakes to exercise no interference in the internal administration of Bhutan. On its part the Government of Bhutan agrees to be guided by the advice of the Government of India in regard to its external relations," the revised treaty now states "In keeping with the abiding ties of close friendship and cooperation between Bhutan and India, the Government of the Kingdom of Bhutan and the Government of the Republic of India shall cooperate closely with each other on issues relating to their national interests. Neither government shall allow the use of its territory for activities harmful to the national security and interest of the other." The revised treaty also includes this preamble: "Reaffirming their respect for each other's independence, sovereignty and territorial integrity", an element absent in the earlier version. By long-standing agreement, Indian and Bhutanese citizens may travel to each other's countries without a <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_passport" title="Bhutanese passport">passport</a> or visa, but must still have their national identity cards. Bhutanese citizens may also work in India without legal restriction. </p>
      <p>Bhutan does not have formal diplomatic ties with China, but exchanges of visits at various levels between them have significantly increased in recent times. The first bilateral agreement between China and Bhutan was signed in 1998 and Bhutan has also set up honorary consulates in the <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_regions_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Special administrative regions of the People's Republic of China">Special Administrative Regions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan's border with China is largely not demarcated and thus disputed in some places. Approximately 269 square kilometers (104&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) remain under discussion between China and Bhutan.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> On 13 November 2005, Chinese soldiers crossed into the disputed territories between China and Bhutan and began building roads and bridges.<sup id="cite_ref-dispcb_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dispcb-96">[96]</a></sup> Bhutanese Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Khandu_Wangchuk" title="Khandu Wangchuk">Khandu Wangchuk</a> took up the matter with Chinese authorities after the issue was raised in the Bhutanese parliament. In response, Foreign Ministry spokesman Qin Gang of the People's Republic of China said that the border remains in dispute and that the two sides are continuing to work for a peaceful and cordial resolution of the dispute, denying that the presence of soldiers in the area was an attempt to forcibly occupy it.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> An Indian intelligence officer said that a Chinese delegation in Bhutan told the Bhutanese they were "overreacting". The Bhutanese newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Kuensel" title="Kuensel">Kuensel</a></i> said that China might use the roads to further Chinese claims along the border.<sup id="cite_ref-dispcb_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dispcb-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan has very warm relations with Japan, which provides significant development assistance. The Bhutanese royals were hosted by the Japanese imperial family during a <a href="/wiki/State_visit" title="State visit">state visit</a> in 2011. Japan is also helping Bhutan cope with glacial floods through developing an early warning system. Bhutan enjoys strong political and diplomatic relations with Bangladesh. The Bhutanese king was the guest of honor during celebrations of the 40th anniversary of Bangladesh's independence.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> A 2014 joint statement by the prime ministers of both countries announced cooperation in areas of hydropower, river management and climate change mitigation.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Bangladesh and Bhutan signed a preferential trade agreement in 2020 with provisions for <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan has diplomatic relations with 53 countries and the European Union and has missions in India, Bangladesh, Thailand, Kuwait and Belgium. It has two UN missions, one in New York and one in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>. Only India, Bangladesh and Kuwait have residential embassies in Bhutan. Other countries maintain informal diplomatic contact via their embassies in <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">Dhaka</a>. Bhutan maintains formal <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bhutan" title="Foreign relations of Bhutan">diplomatic relations</a> with several Asian and European nations, Canada, and Brazil. Other countries, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Bhutan–United States relations">such as the United States</a> and the United Kingdom, have no formal diplomatic relations with Bhutan but maintain informal contact through their respective embassies in <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a> and the Bhutanese honorary consulate in Washington, DC. The United Kingdom has an honorary consul resident in Thimphu.The latest country with which Bhutan has established diplomatic relations is Israel, on 12 December 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-state_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-103">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">

        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>Bhutan opposed the Russian annexation of Crimea in <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262">United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262</a>. </p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Bhutan" title="Military of Bhutan">Military of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bhutan_Army" title="Royal Bhutan Army">Royal Bhutan Army</a> is Bhutan's military service and is the weakest armed forces, according to the Global Firepower survey. It includes the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bodyguard_of_Bhutan" title="Royal Bodyguard of Bhutan">royal bodyguard</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bhutan_Police" title="Royal Bhutan Police">Royal Bhutan Police</a>. Membership is voluntary and the minimum age for recruitment is 18. The standing army numbers about 16,000 and is trained by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">Indian Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> It has an annual budget of about US$13.7&nbsp;million (1.8 percent of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>). As a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a>, Bhutan has no navy. It also has no air force or army aviation corps. The Army relies on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Air_Command_(India)" title="Eastern Air Command (India)">Eastern Air Command</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">Indian Air Force</a> for air assistance. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Bhutan" title="Human rights in Bhutan">Human rights in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Bhutan" title="LGBT rights in Bhutan">LGBT rights in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jakar_tshechu,_dancers_(15222929514).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Jakar_tshechu%2C_dancers_%2815222929514%29.jpg/220px-Jakar_tshechu%2C_dancers_%2815222929514%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Jakar_tshechu%2C_dancers_%2815222929514%29.jpg/330px-Jakar_tshechu%2C_dancers_%2815222929514%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Jakar_tshechu%2C_dancers_%2815222929514%29.jpg/440px-Jakar_tshechu%2C_dancers_%2815222929514%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jakar_tshechu,_dancers_(15222929514).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Women of Bhutan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan is ranked as "Partly Free" by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Bhutan's parliament decriminalized homosexuality in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Women in Bhutan tend to be less active in politics than men due to customs and aspects of Bhutan's culture that dictate a woman's role in the household.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-107">[107]</a></sup> This leads to a limitation of their voices in government. Bhutan has made steps toward gender equality by enrolling more girls in school as well as creating the "National Commission for Women and Children" (NCWC) in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-:13_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-108">[108]</a></sup> This program was created to promote and protect women's and children's rights. Bhutan also elected its first female <i>Dzongda</i>, equivalent to a District Attorney, in 2012, and its first female minister in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-:13_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-108">[108]</a></sup> Minister Dorji Choden, chair for the National Commission for Women and Children, believes that the aforementioned program can be used to "promote women into more leadership roles" which can then lead women to take on more active roles in their society.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-107">[107]</a></sup> Overall there has also been a gradual increase in women in power with a 68% increase in women representation from 2011 to 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-:13_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s_refugee_crisis">1990s refugee crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 1990s refugee crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Starting in the 1980s, a part of Bhutan's minority population groups of <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a> speakers ("<a href="/wiki/Lhotshampa" title="Lhotshampa">Lhotshampa</a>"), in Southern Bhutan, fell victim to perceived political persecution by the Bhutanese government as part of what they viewed as Bhutanization (termed One Nation, One People) policy which was aimed to nationalize the country. <sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sinha_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sinha-110">[110]</a></sup> In 1977 followed by in 1985, Bhutan's government enacted legislations which impacted the Lhotshampa ethnic minority. The review of the national citizenship criteria and provisions for denationalization of illegally present population in the country ensued.<sup id="cite_ref-seattletimes.com_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattletimes.com-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Bhutanese_Refugee_Si_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Bhutanese_Refugee_Si-112">[112]</a></sup> The government enforced uniformity in dress and language to create a national identity which was aligned with the majority <a href="/wiki/Ngalop_people" title="Ngalop people">Drukpa</a> culture of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theweek11_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theweek11-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIDCM_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIDCM-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unhcr08_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr08-115">[115]</a></sup> The Lhotshampas started demonstrations in protest of such discriminatory laws, voicing for a change to be brought to the existing political system towards a preferred multi-party democracy. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.amnesty.org/download/Documents/184000/asa140041994en.pdf">[2]</a> These demonstrations turned into violence when some ethnic Nepalese attacked government officials and burned schools in the southern districts. <sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Consequently, such political demonstrations were suppressed by Bhutanese security forces. As a result, members of Bhutanese police and army are accused of imprisonment and torture of many who were politically active in such demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Subsequent allegations of Lhotshampas being targeted, houses being burned, and being expelled from the country with their property confiscated without compensation were reported.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-118">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This escalated up until the early 1990s, and was followed by deportations of suspected immigrants and people who were involved in the revolt against the state. The revolt mirrored images of the <a href="/wiki/Gorkhaland_movement" title="Gorkhaland movement">Gorkhaland movement</a> stirring up in the neighboring states of Assam and West Bengal at the same time, and fueled up fears of a fate similar to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sikkim" title="Kingdom of Sikkim">Kingdom of Sikkim</a> where immigrant Nepalis population had overwhelmed the small native population of the kingdom, leading to its demise as an independent nation.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The Bhutanese security forces in doing so were accused of human rights violations including torture and rape of political demonstrators, and some Lhotshampas were accused of staging a violent revolt against the state.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Bhutanese_Refugee_Si_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Bhutanese_Refugee_Si-112">[112]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a>, an estimate of 107,000 <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_refugees" title="Bhutanese refugees">Bhutanese refugees</a> living in seven camps in eastern Nepal have been documented as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-unhcr08_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr08-115">[115]</a></sup> After many years in refugee camps, many inhabitants moved to other host nations such as Canada, Norway, the UK, Australia, and the US as refugees. The US admitted 60,773 refugees from fiscal years 2008 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-120">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Nepal" title="Government of Nepal">Nepalese government</a> refused to assimilate the Bhutanese refugees (Lhotshampas) and did not allow a legal path to citizenship, so they were left stateless.<sup id="cite_ref-hrr_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrr-121">[121]</a></sup> Careful scrutiny has been used to review the status of the refugee's relatives in the country, and citizenship identity cards and voting rights for these reviewed people are restricted.<sup id="cite_ref-hrr_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrr-121">[121]</a></sup> Bhutan does not recognize political parties associated with these refugees and see them as a threat to the well-being of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-hrr_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrr-121">[121]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_group" title="Human rights group">Human rights group's</a> rhetoric that the government interfered with individual rights by requiring all citizens, including ethnic minority members, to wear the traditional dress of the ethnic majority in public places was used as political tool for the demonstrations. The Bhutanese government since then enforced the law of national attire to be worn in Buddhist religious buildings, government offices, schools, official functions, and public ceremonies aimed towards preserving and promoting the national identity of Bhutan.<sup id="cite_ref-hrr_121-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrr-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg/220px-Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg/330px-Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg/440px-Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1383" data-file-height="892"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ethnic Nepalese ("<a href="/wiki/Lhotshampa" title="Lhotshampa">Lhotshampa</a>") migrants that were forcefully expelled from Bhutan, and arrived in Nepal in the early 1990s.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>The kingdom has been accused of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Bhutan" title="Freedom of religion in Bhutan">banning religious proselytizing</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> which critics deem as a violation of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> and a policy of ethnic cleansing.<sup id="cite_ref-Bhutan's_ethnic_cleansing_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bhutan's_ethnic_cleansing-124">[124]</a></sup> Starting in the 1980s, Bhutan adopted a policy of "One Nation One People" to create a unified sense of national identity. This was interpreted as cultural (in language, dress and religion) and political dominance of the majority <a href="/wiki/Ngalop_people" title="Ngalop people">Drukpa</a> people by the Nepali-speaking people.<sup id="cite_ref-Bhutan_Is_No_Shangri-La_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bhutan_Is_No_Shangri-La-125">[125]</a></sup> Inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Gorkhaland_movement" title="Gorkhaland movement">Gorkhaland Movement</a> and fueled by a sense of injustice, some Lhotshampas began organizing demonstrations against the Bhutanese state. Furthermore, the removal of <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a> language in school curriculum to adopt a more centralized language in <a href="/wiki/Dzongkha" title="Dzongkha">Dzongkha</a> coupled with the denial of citizenship to those who were not able to prove officially issued land holding title prior to 1950<sup id="cite_ref-The_Seattle_Times_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Seattle_Times-126">[126]</a></sup> was perceived as specifically targeting Lhotshampa population estimated to be one-third of the population at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Bhutan_insurgencies_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Bhutan_insurgencies-127">[127]</a></sup> This resulted in widespread unrest and political demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-seattletimes.com_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattletimes.com-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mar.umd.edu_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mar.umd.edu-128">[128]</a></sup> In response to this threat, in 1988, the Bhutanese authorities carried out a special census<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-129">[129]</a></sup> in southern Bhutan to review the status of legal residents from illegal immigrants. This region with high Lhotshampa population had to be legally verified, and the following census led to the deportation these Lhotshampas, estimated to be one-sixth of the total population at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Watch_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Watch-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Director,_Refugee_and_Migrant_Right_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Director,_Refugee_and_Migrant_Right-131">[131]</a></sup> People who had been granted citizenship by the Bhutanese <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_Citizenship_Act_1958" title="Bhutanese Citizenship Act 1958">1958 Nationality Law</a> were also stripped of their citizenship. The state intervened after violence was instigated by some Nepali-speaking citizens in radical form of attacking government officials and burning of schools. <sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Members of Bhutanese police and army were accused of burning Lhotshampa houses, land confiscation and other widespread human rights abuses including arrest, torture and rape of Lhotshampas involved in political protests and violence.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Bhutanese_Refugee_Si_112-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Bhutanese_Refugee_Si-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-133">[133]</a></sup> Following forcible deportation from Bhutan, Lhotshampas spent almost two decades in refugee camps in <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> and were resettled in various western countries such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> between 2007 and 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Lhotshampas_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lhotshampas-134">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_divisions">Political divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Political divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Bhutan" title="Districts of Bhutan">Districts of Bhutan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gewogs_of_Bhutan" title="Gewogs of Bhutan">Gewogs of Bhutan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_of_Bhutan_2009" title="Local Government Act of Bhutan 2009">Local Government Act of Bhutan 2009</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan is divided into twenty <i><a href="/wiki/Dzongkhag" class="mw-redirect" title="Dzongkhag">Dzongkhag</a></i> (districts), administered by a body called the Dzongkhag Tshogdu. In certain <i><a href="/wiki/Thromde" title="Thromde">thromdes</a></i> (urban municipalities), a further municipal administration is directly subordinate to the Dzongkhag administration. In the vast majority of constituencies, rural <i><a href="/wiki/Gewogs_of_Bhutan" title="Gewogs of Bhutan">geog</a></i> (village blocks) are administered by bodies called the Geog Tshogde.<sup id="cite_ref-LGA09_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGA09-135">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Thromdes (municipalities) elect Thrompons to lead administration, who in turn represent the Thromde in the Dzongkhag Tshogdu. Likewise, <i>geog</i> elect headmen called <i>gup</i>s, vice-headmen called <i>mangmis</i>, who also sit on the Dzongkhag Tshogdu, as well as other members of the Geog Tshogde. The basis of electoral constituencies in Bhutan is the <i><a href="/wiki/Chiwog" class="mw-redirect" title="Chiwog">chiwog</a></i>, a subdivision of gewogs delineated by the Election Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-LGA09_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGA09-135">[135]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="noresize thumb tright" style=";">
