         <td>9. <a href="/wiki/Pemagatshel_District" title="Pemagatshel District">Pemagatshel</a> </td> 
         <td>
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1009628807"><span class="uchen" style="font-size:1.25em; vertical-align:middle; word-wrap:break-word;">པད་མ་དགའ་ཚལ་རྫོང་ཁག་</span> </td> 
         <td>19. <a href="/wiki/Wangdue_Phodrang_District" title="Wangdue Phodrang District">Wangdue Phodrang</a> </td> 
         <td>
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1009628807"><span class="uchen" style="font-size:1.25em; vertical-align:middle; word-wrap:break-word;">དབང་འདུས་ཕོ་བྲང་རྫོང་ཁག་</span> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr align="left"> 
         <td style="background:#f0f0f0">10. <a href="/wiki/Punakha_District" title="Punakha District">Punakha</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#f0f0f0">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1009628807"><span class="uchen" style="font-size:1.25em; vertical-align:middle; word-wrap:break-word;">སྤུ་ན་ཁ་རྫོང་ཁག་</span> </td> 
         <td style="background:#f0f0f0">20. <a href="/wiki/Zhemgang_District" title="Zhemgang District">Zhemgang</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#f0f0f0">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1009628807"><span class="uchen" style="font-size:1.25em; vertical-align:middle; word-wrap:break-word;">གཞམས་སྒང་རྫོང་ཁག་</span> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bhutan.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Tree_map_export_2009_Bhutan.jpeg/350px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bhutan.jpeg" decoding="async" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Tree_map_export_2009_Bhutan.jpeg/525px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bhutan.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Tree_map_export_2009_Bhutan.jpeg/700px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bhutan.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="863"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bhutan.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Bhutan's exports.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_Power_Corporation_office_Thimphu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bhutan_Power_Corporation_office_Thimphu.jpg/220px-Bhutan_Power_Corporation_office_Thimphu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bhutan_Power_Corporation_office_Thimphu.jpg/330px-Bhutan_Power_Corporation_office_Thimphu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bhutan_Power_Corporation_office_Thimphu.jpg/440px-Bhutan_Power_Corporation_office_Thimphu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_Power_Corporation_office_Thimphu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Bhutan Power Corporation headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Thimphu" title="Thimphu">Thimphu</a>. Bhutan's principal export is <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Bhutan" title="Economy of Bhutan">Economy of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan's currency is the <a href="/wiki/Ngultrum" class="mw-redirect" title="Ngultrum">ngultrum</a>, whose value is <a href="/wiki/Fixed_exchange_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fixed exchange rate">fixed</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">Indian rupee</a>. The rupee is also accepted as <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal tender</a> in the country. Though Bhutan's economy is one of the world's smallest,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> it has grown rapidly in recent years, by eight percent in 2005 and 14 percent in 2006. In 2007, Bhutan had the second-fastest-growing economy in the world, with an annual economic growth rate of 22.4 percent. This was mainly due to the commissioning of the gigantic <a href="/wiki/Tala_Hydroelectric_Power_Station" title="Tala Hydroelectric Power Station">Tala Hydroelectric Power Station</a>. As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Bhutan's <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> was US$2,420.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan's economy is based on agriculture, forestry, tourism and the sale of <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric power">hydroelectric power</a> to India. Agriculture provides the main livelihood for 55.4 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Agrarian practices consist largely of <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_farming" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsistence farming">subsistence farming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a>. Handicrafts, particularly weaving and the manufacture of religious art for home altars, are a small <a href="/wiki/Cottage_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Cottage industry">cottage industry</a>. A landscape that varies from hilly to ruggedly mountainous has made the building of roads and other infrastructure difficult and expensive. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bridges_at_Panbang_2019-12-13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bridges_at_Panbang_2019-12-13.jpg/220px-Bridges_at_Panbang_2019-12-13.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bridges_at_Panbang_2019-12-13.jpg/330px-Bridges_at_Panbang_2019-12-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bridges_at_Panbang_2019-12-13.jpg/440px-Bridges_at_Panbang_2019-12-13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8256" data-file-height="5504"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bridges_at_Panbang_2019-12-13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Modern and traditional bridges over a river in Panbang
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>This, and a lack of access to the sea, has meant that Bhutan has not been able to benefit from significant trading of its produce. Bhutan has no <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">railways</a>, though <a href="/wiki/Indian_Railways" title="Indian Railways">Indian Railways</a> plans to link southern Bhutan to its vast network under an agreement signed in January 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Bhutan and India signed a 'free trade' accord in 2008, which additionally allowed Bhutanese imports and exports from third markets to transit India without tariffs.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Bhutan had trade relations with the <a href="/wiki/Tibet_Autonomous_Region" title="Tibet Autonomous Region">Tibet Autonomous Region</a> of China until 1960, when it closed its border with China after an influx of refugees.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Bhutan is much higher than world average. In 2016, Bhutan had 5.0 global hectares <sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-143">[143]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, much more than the world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> In 2016 Bhutan used 4.5 global hectares of biocapacity per person - their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use less biocapacity than Bhutan contains. As a result, Bhutan is running a biocapacity reserve.<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-143">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The industrial sector is currently in a nascent stage. Although most production comes from cottage industry, larger industries are being encouraged and some industries such as cement, steel, and <a href="/wiki/Ferroalloy" title="Ferroalloy">ferroalloy</a> have been set up. Most development projects, such as road construction, rely on <a href="/wiki/Contract_labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Contract labor">contract labor</a> from neighboring India. Agricultural produce includes rice, chilies, dairy (some yak, mostly cow) products, buckwheat, barley, root crops, apples, and citrus and maize at lower elevations. Industries include cement, wood products, processed fruits, alcoholic beverages and <a href="/wiki/Calcium_carbide" title="Calcium carbide">calcium carbide</a>. </p>
      <p>Bhutan has seen recent growth in the technology sector, in areas such as green tech and consumer Internet/e-commerce.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In May 2012, "Thimphu TechPark" was launched in the capital. It incubates <a href="/wiki/Startups" class="mw-redirect" title="Startups">startups</a> via the "Bhutan Innovation and Technology Center" (BITC).<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Incomes of over <a href="/wiki/Ngultrum" class="mw-redirect" title="Ngultrum">Nu</a> 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Per_annum" title="Per annum">per annum</a> are taxed, but as Bhutan is currently one of the world's least developed countries, very few wage and salary earners qualify. Bhutan's inflation rate was estimated at about three percent in 2003. Bhutan has a <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> of around US$5.855&nbsp;billion (adjusted to <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>), making it the 158th-largest economy in the world. Per capita income (PPP) is around $7,641,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-63">[63]</a></sup> ranked 144th. Government revenues total $407.1&nbsp;million, though expenditures amount to $614&nbsp;million. Twenty-five percent of the budget expenditure, however, is financed by India's Ministry of External Affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[note 1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan's exports, principally electricity, <a href="/wiki/Cardamom" title="Cardamom">cardamom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a>, timber, handicrafts, cement, fruit, precious stones and spices, total €128&nbsp;million (2000 est.). Imports, however, amount to €164&nbsp;million, leading to a <a href="/wiki/Trade_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade deficit">trade deficit</a>. Main items imported include fuel and lubricants, grain, machinery, vehicles, fabrics and rice. Bhutan's main export partner is India, accounting for 58.6 percent of its export goods. Hong Kong (30.1 percent) and Bangladesh (7.3 percent) are the other two top export partners.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-63">[63]</a></sup> As its border with Tibet Autonomous Region is closed, trade between Bhutan and China is now almost non-existent. Bhutan's import partners include India (74.5 percent), Japan (7.4 percent) and Sweden (3.2 percent). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Bhutan" title="Agriculture in Bhutan">Agriculture in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_Field_-_IMG_3815.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bhutan_Field_-_IMG_3815.JPG/220px-Bhutan_Field_-_IMG_3815.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bhutan_Field_-_IMG_3815.JPG/330px-Bhutan_Field_-_IMG_3815.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bhutan_Field_-_IMG_3815.JPG/440px-Bhutan_Field_-_IMG_3815.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_Field_-_IMG_3815.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rice terraces in one of Bhutan's fertile valleys.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The share of the agricultural sector in GDP declined from approximately 55% in 1985 to 33% in 2003. In 2013 the government announced the aspiration that Bhutan will become the first country in the world with 100 percent <a href="/wiki/Organic_farming" title="Organic farming">organic farming</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_red_rice" title="Bhutanese red rice">Bhutanese red rice</a> is the country's most widely known agricultural export, enjoying a market in North America and Europe. Bangladesh is the largest market of Bhutanese <a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">apples</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Fishing_in_Bhutan" title="Fishing in Bhutan">Fishing in Bhutan</a> is mainly centered on <a href="/wiki/Trout" title="Trout">trout</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carp" title="Carp">carp</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BDFC-SDF_Bulding_Thimphu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/BDFC-SDF_Bulding_Thimphu.jpg/220px-BDFC-SDF_Bulding_Thimphu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/BDFC-SDF_Bulding_Thimphu.jpg/330px-BDFC-SDF_Bulding_Thimphu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/BDFC-SDF_Bulding_Thimphu.jpg/440px-BDFC-SDF_Bulding_Thimphu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4458" data-file-height="2953"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BDFC-SDF_Bulding_Thimphu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Office of the <a href="/wiki/SAARC" class="mw-redirect" title="SAARC">SAARC</a> Development Fund in Thimphu
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The industrial sector accounts for 22% of the economy. The key manufacturing sectors in Bhutan include production of <a href="/wiki/Ferroalloy" title="Ferroalloy">ferroalloy</a>, cement, metal poles, iron and nonalloy steel products, processed <a href="/wiki/Graphite" title="Graphite">graphite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper_conductor" title="Copper conductor">copper conductors</a>, alcoholic and carbonated <a href="/wiki/Beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Beverage">beverages</a>, processed fruits, carpets, wood products and furniture.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Bhutan" title="Mining in Bhutan">Mining in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan has deposits of numerous minerals. Commercial production includes <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolomite_(rock)" title="Dolomite (rock)">dolomite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>. The country has proven reserves of <a href="/wiki/Beryl" title="Beryl">beryl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, graphite, <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mica" title="Mica">mica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyrite" title="Pyrite">pyrite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">tungsten</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>. However, the country's mineral deposits remain untapped, as it prefers to conserve the environment, rather than to exploit and destroy it for money.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_electricity_production.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Bhutan_electricity_production.svg/220px-Bhutan_electricity_production.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Bhutan_electricity_production.svg/330px-Bhutan_electricity_production.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Bhutan_electricity_production.svg/440px-Bhutan_electricity_production.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_electricity_production.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bhutan electricity production by year
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Bhutan" title="Energy in Bhutan">Energy in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan's largest export is hydroelectricity. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it generates about 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Watt" title="Watt">MW</a> of hydropower from <a href="/wiki/Himalaya" class="mw-redirect" title="Himalaya">Himalayan</a> river valleys.<sup id="cite_ref-en.prothom-alo.com_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.prothom-alo.com-154">[153]</a></sup> The country has a potential to generate 30,000 MW of hydropower.<sup id="cite_ref-en.prothom-alo.com_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.prothom-alo.com-154">[153]</a></sup> Power is supplied to various states in India. Future projects are being planned with Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-en.prothom-alo.com_154-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.prothom-alo.com-154">[153]</a></sup> Hydropower has been the primary focus for the country's <a href="/wiki/Five-Year_Plans_of_Bhutan" title="Five-Year Plans of Bhutan">five-year plans</a>. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Tala_Hydroelectric_Power_Station" title="Tala Hydroelectric Power Station">Tala Hydroelectric Power Station</a> is its largest power plant, with an installed capacity of 1,020 MW. It has received assistance from India, Austria and the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> in developing hydroelectric projects. Besides hydropower, it is also endowed with significant renewable energy resources such as solar, wind and bioenergy. Technically viable solar energy generation capacity is around 12,000 MW and wind around 760 MW. More than 70% of its land is under forest cover, which is an immense source of bioenergy in the country.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan is likely to benefit geopolitically from the global transition to renewable energy and is ranked no. 4 out of 156 nations in the index of geopolitical gains and losses after energy transition (GeGaLo Index).<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_sector">Financial sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Financial sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Le_Meridien_Hotel,_Thimphu_(c).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Le_Meridien_Hotel%2C_Thimphu_%28c%29.jpg/220px-Le_Meridien_Hotel%2C_Thimphu_%28c%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Le_Meridien_Hotel%2C_Thimphu_%28c%29.jpg/330px-Le_Meridien_Hotel%2C_Thimphu_%28c%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Le_Meridien_Hotel%2C_Thimphu_%28c%29.jpg/440px-Le_Meridien_Hotel%2C_Thimphu_%28c%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4912" data-file-height="5172"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Le_Meridien_Hotel,_Thimphu_(c).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Le_M%C3%A9ridien" title="Le Méridien">Le Méridien</a> <a href="/wiki/Thimphu" title="Thimphu">Thimphu</a> is part of Bhutan's burgeoning <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Bhutan" title="Tourism in Bhutan">tourism industry</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Banking_in_Bhutan" title="Banking in Bhutan">Banking in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are Five Commercial Banks in the country and two largest banks are the Bank of Bhutan and the Bhutan National Bank which are based in Thimphu. Other commercial banks are Bhutan Development Bank, T-Bank and Druk Punjab National Bank. The country's financial sector is also supported by other non-banking Financial Institutions. They are Royal Insurance Corporation of Bhutan (RICB), National Pension and Provident Fund (NPPF), and Bhutan Insurance Limited (BIL). The central bank of the country is the Royal Monetary Authority of Bhutan (RMA). The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Securities_Exchange_of_Bhutan" title="Royal Securities Exchange of Bhutan">Royal Securities Exchange of Bhutan</a> is the main <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/SAARC" class="mw-redirect" title="SAARC">SAARC</a> Development Fund is based in Thimphu.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Bhutan" title="Tourism in Bhutan">Tourism in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2014, Bhutan welcomed 133,480 foreign visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> Seeking to become a high-value destination, it imposes a daily fee of anywhere between US$180 to US$290 per day (or more) on tourists that covers touring and hotel accommodation.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> The industry employs 21,000 people and accounts for 1.8% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> However the Bhutanese goal of attracting high value tourists can be criticized for actually only attracting wealthy tourists and poses the question on whether by definition "high quality" actually means "rich".<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country currently has no <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Sites">UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a>, but it has eight declared tentative sites for UNESCO inclusion since 2012. These sites include: Ancient Ruin of <a href="/wiki/Drukgyel_Dzong" class="mw-redirect" title="Drukgyel Dzong">Drukgyel Dzong</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bumdelling_Wildlife_Sanctuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Bumdelling Wildlife Sanctuary">Bumdelling Wildlife Sanctuary</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dzongs" class="mw-redirect" title="Dzongs">Dzongs</a>: the centre of temporal and religious authorities (<a href="/wiki/Punakha_Dzong" title="Punakha Dzong">Punakha Dzong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wangdue_Phodrang_Dzong" class="mw-redirect" title="Wangdue Phodrang Dzong">Wangdue Phodrang Dzong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paro_Dzong" class="mw-redirect" title="Paro Dzong">Paro Dzong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trongsa_Dzong" title="Trongsa Dzong">Trongsa Dzong</a> and Dagana Dzong),<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jigme_Dorji_National_Park" title="Jigme Dorji National Park">Jigme Dorji National Park</a> (JDNP),<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Royal_Manas_National_Park" title="Royal Manas National Park">Royal Manas National Park</a> (RMNP),<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> Sacred Sites associated with <a href="/wiki/Phajo_Drugom_Zhigpo" title="Phajo Drugom Zhigpo">Phajo Drugom Zhigpo</a> and his descendants,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sakteng_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Sakteng Wildlife Sanctuary">Sakteng Wildlife Sanctuary</a> (SWS),<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tamzhing_Monastery" title="Tamzhing Monastery">Tamzhing Monastery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> Bhutan also has numerous tourist sites that are not included in its UNESCO tentative list. Bhutan has one element, the <i>Mask dance of the drums from Drametse</i>, registered in the UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage List.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan is also well known for mountain adventure trekking and hiking. Jhomolhari Base Camp Trek, Snowman Trek, and Masagang trek are some of the popular treks in Bhutan. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Bhutan" title="Transport in Bhutan">Transport in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Paro_day_1-58_(8202279871).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Paro_day_1-58_%288202279871%29.jpg/220px-Paro_day_1-58_%288202279871%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Paro_day_1-58_%288202279871%29.jpg/330px-Paro_day_1-58_%288202279871%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Paro_day_1-58_%288202279871%29.jpg/440px-Paro_day_1-58_%288202279871%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Paro_day_1-58_(8202279871).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Druk_Air" title="Druk Air">Druk Air</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a> in <a href="/wiki/Paro_Airport" title="Paro Airport">Paro Airport</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Paro_Airport" title="Paro Airport">Paro Airport</a> is the only international airport in Bhutan. <a href="/wiki/Yongphulla_Airport" title="Yongphulla Airport">Yongphulla Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Trashigang" title="Trashigang">Trashigang</a> is a small domestic airport that underwent upgrades through 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> Yonphula Domestic Airport was scheduled for completion in January 2010 but as of January&nbsp;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the airport remains closed due to ongoing runway repair.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> National carrier Druk Air operates flights between Paro Airport and airports in <a href="/wiki/Jakar" title="Jakar">Jakar</a> (Bumthang Dzongkhag) and <a href="/wiki/Gelephu" title="Gelephu">Gelephu</a> (Sarpang Dzongkhag) on a weekly basis.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Lateral_Road" title="Lateral Road">Lateral Road</a> is Bhutan's primary east–west corridor, connecting the towns of <a href="/wiki/Phuentsholing" class="mw-redirect" title="Phuentsholing">Phuentsholing</a> in the southwest to <a href="/wiki/Trashigang" title="Trashigang">Trashigang</a> in the east. Notable settlements that the Lateral Road runs through directly are <a href="/wiki/Wangdue_Phodrang" title="Wangdue Phodrang">Wangdue Phodrang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trongsa" title="Trongsa">Trongsa</a>. The Lateral Road also has spurs connecting to the capital <a href="/wiki/Thimphu" title="Thimphu">Thimphu</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Population_center" class="mw-redirect" title="Population center">population centers</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Paro,_Bhutan" title="Paro, Bhutan">Paro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punakha" title="Punakha">Punakha</a>. As with other roads in Bhutan, the Lateral Road presents serious safety concerns due to pavement conditions, sheer drops, hairpin turns, weather and landslides.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 2014, road widening has been a priority across Bhutan, in particular for the north-east–west highway from Trashigang to Dochula. The widening project is expected to be completed by the end of 2017 and will make road travel across the country substantially faster and more efficient. In addition, it is projected that the improved road conditions will encourage more tourism in the more inaccessible eastern region of Bhutan.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> Currently, the road conditions appear to be deterring tourists from visiting Bhutan due to the increased instances of road blocks, landslides and dust disruption caused by the widening project.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Although Bhutan currently has no railways, it has entered into an agreement with India to link southern Bhutan to India's vast network by constructing an 18-kilometer-long (11&nbsp;mi), <span class="nowrap">1,676&nbsp;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">5&nbsp;ft&nbsp;6&nbsp;in</span>) <a href="/wiki/Indian_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian gauge">broad gauge</a> rail link between <a href="/wiki/Hashimara" class="mw-redirect" title="Hashimara">Hashimara</a> in West Bengal and Toribari in Bhutan. The construction of the railway via Satali, Bharna Bari and Dalsingpara by <a href="/wiki/Indian_railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian railways">Indian railways</a> will be funded by India.<sup id="cite_ref-times2009_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times2009-182">[181]</a></sup> Bhutan's nearest railway station is Hasimara. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Bhutan" title="Demographics of Bhutan">Demographics of Bhutan</a>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutanese_people.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Bhutanese_people.jpg/220px-Bhutanese_people.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Bhutanese_people.jpg/330px-Bhutanese_people.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Bhutanese_people.jpg/440px-Bhutanese_people.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a>

      <p>Bhutan had a population of 754,388 people in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-4">[4]</a></sup> Bhutan has a median age of 24.8 years.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_63-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-63">[63]</a></sup> There are 1,070 males to every 1,000 females. The literacy rate in Bhutan is 59.5 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Bhutanese people primarily consist of the <a href="/wiki/Ngalop" class="mw-redirect" title="Ngalop">Ngalops</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sharchop_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharchop people">Sharchops</a>, called the Western Bhutanese and Eastern Bhutanese respectively. Although the <a href="/wiki/Sharchops" title="Sharchops">Sharchops</a> are slightly larger in demographic size, the Ngalops dominate the political sphere, as the King and the political elite belong to this group.<sup id="cite_ref-growup3_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-growup3-184">[183]</a></sup> The Ngalops primarily consist of Bhutanese living in the western part of the country. Their culture is closely related to that of Tibet. Much the same could be said of the Sharchops, the largest group, who traditionally follow the <a href="/wiki/Nyingmapa" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyingmapa">Nyingmapa</a> rather than the official <a href="/wiki/Drukpa_Kagyu" class="mw-redirect" title="Drukpa Kagyu">Drukpa Kagyu</a> form of <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism" title="Tibetan Buddhism">Tibetan Buddhism</a>. In modern times, with improved transportation infrastructure, there has been much intermarriage between these groups. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Lhotshampa" title="Lhotshampa">Lhotshampa</a>, meaning "southerner Bhutanese", are a heterogeneous group of mostly <a href="/wiki/People_of_Nepal" class="mw-redirect" title="People of Nepal">Nepalese</a> ancestry who have sought political and cultural recognition including equality in right to abode, language, and dress. Unofficial estimates claimed that they constituted 45% of the population in the 1988 census.<sup id="cite_ref-bns_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bns-185">[184]</a></sup> Starting in the 1980s, Bhutan adopted a policy of "One Nation One People" to exert cultural (in language, dress and religion) and political dominance of the majority Drukpa people.<sup id="cite_ref-Bhutan_Is_No_Shangri-La_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bhutan_Is_No_Shangri-La-125">[125]</a></sup> The policy manifested in banning of teaching of <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a> language in schools and denial of citizenship to those who were not able to prove officially issued land holding title prior to 1950<sup id="cite_ref-The_Seattle_Times_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Seattle_Times-126">[126]</a></sup> specifically targeting ethnic Nepali-speaking minority groups ("<a href="/wiki/Lhotshampa" title="Lhotshampa">Lhotshampa</a>"), representing one-third of the population at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Bhutan_insurgencies_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Bhutan_insurgencies-127">[127]</a></sup> This resulted in widespread unrest and political demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-seattletimes.com_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattletimes.com-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mar.umd.edu_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mar.umd.edu-128">[128]</a></sup> In 1988, the Bhutanese authorities carried out a special census<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-129">[129]</a></sup> in southern Bhutan, region of high <a href="/wiki/Lhotshampa" title="Lhotshampa">Lhotshampa</a> population, resulting in mass denationalization of <a href="/wiki/Lhotshampas" class="mw-redirect" title="Lhotshampas">Lhotshampas</a>, followed by forcible deportation of 107,000 <a href="/wiki/Lhotshampas" class="mw-redirect" title="Lhotshampas">Lhotshampas</a>, approximately one-sixth of the total population at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Watch_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Watch-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Director,_Refugee_and_Migrant_Right_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Director,_Refugee_and_Migrant_Right-131">[131]</a></sup> Those who had been granted citizenship by the <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_Citizenship_Act_1958" title="Bhutanese Citizenship Act 1958">1958 Nationality Law</a> were stripped of their citizenship. Members of Bhutanese police and army were involved in burning of <a href="/wiki/Lhotshampa" title="Lhotshampa">Lhotshampa</a> houses, land confiscation and other widespread human rights abuses including arrest, torture and rape of <a href="/wiki/Lhotshampas" class="mw-redirect" title="Lhotshampas">Lhotshampas</a> involved in political protests.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Bhutanese_Refugee_Si_112-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Bhutanese_Refugee_Si-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-133">[133]</a></sup> Following forcible deportation from Bhutan, <a href="/wiki/Lhotshampas" class="mw-redirect" title="Lhotshampas">Lhotshampas</a> spent almost two decades in refugee camps in <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> and were resettled in various western countries such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> between 2007 and 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Lhotshampas_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lhotshampas-134">[134]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities_and_towns">Cities and towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cities and towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Bhutan" title="List of cities in Bhutan">List of cities in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Thimphu" title="Thimphu">Thimphu</a>, the largest city and capital of Bhutan.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Damphu,_Tsirang" title="Damphu, Tsirang">Damphu</a>, the administrative headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Tsirang_District" title="Tsirang District">Tsirang District</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jakar" title="Jakar">Jakar</a>, the administrative headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Bumthang_District" title="Bumthang District">Bumthang District</a> and the place where Buddhism entered Bhutan.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Mongar" title="Mongar">Mongar</a>, the eastern commercial hub of the country.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Paro,_Bhutan" title="Paro, Bhutan">Paro</a>, site of the <a href="/wiki/Paro_Airport" title="Paro Airport">international airport</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Phuentsholing" class="mw-redirect" title="Phuentsholing">Phuentsholing</a>, Bhutan's commercial hub.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Punakha" title="Punakha">Punakha</a>, the old capital.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Samdrup_Jongkhar" title="Samdrup Jongkhar">Samdrup Jongkhar</a>, the southeastern town on the border with India.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Trashigang" title="Trashigang">Trashigang</a>, administrative headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Trashigang_District" title="Trashigang District">Trashigang District</a>, the most populous district in the country.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Trongsa" title="Trongsa">Trongsa</a>, in central Bhutan, which has the largest and the most magnificent of all the <a href="/wiki/Dzongs" class="mw-redirect" title="Dzongs">dzongs</a> in Bhutan.</li>
      </ul>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Magenta"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 15915.284869129px; border-left-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 7957.3282711643px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 2272.175778494px; border-left-color:GreenYellow"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:GreenYellow"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:GreenYellow"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 606.67925626074px; border-left-color:Orange"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Orange"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Orange"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:99.992104420382px 1.2566039883353px 0 0; border-top-color:Yellow"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Yellow"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bhutan" title="Religion in Bhutan">Religion in Bhutan</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (June 2019)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (Pew 2010)<sup id="cite_ref-pew2010_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew2010-187">[186]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Yellow; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (<a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">State religion</a>) (74.8%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Orange; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (22.6%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:GreenYellow; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Bon" title="Bon">Bon</a> and other indigenous faith (1.9%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (0.5%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Green; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (0.1%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Magenta; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Other or none (0.2%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bhutan" title="Religion in Bhutan">Religion in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>It is estimated that between two-thirds and three-quarters of the Bhutanese population follow <a href="/wiki/Vajrayana_Buddhism" class="mw-redirect" title="Vajrayana Buddhism">Vajrayana Buddhism</a>, which is also the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>. About one-quarter to one-third are followers of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>. Other religions account for less than 1% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-USDOS_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USDOS-188">[187]</a></sup> The current legal framework, in principle guarantees <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>; <a href="/wiki/Proselytism" title="Proselytism">proselytism</a>, however, is forbidden by a royal government decision<sup id="cite_ref-USDOS_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USDOS-188">[187]</a></sup> and by judicial interpretation of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bhutan" title="Constitution of Bhutan">Constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Buddhism was introduced to Bhutan in the 7th century AD. Tibetan king <a href="/wiki/Songts%C3%A4n_Gampo" class="mw-redirect" title="Songtsän Gampo">Songtsän Gampo</a> (reigned 627–649), a convert to Buddhism, ordered the construction of two Buddhist temples, at <a href="/wiki/Bumthang_(town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bumthang (town)">Bumthang</a> in central Bhutan and at Kyichu Lhakhang (near <a href="/wiki/Paro,_Bhutan" title="Paro, Bhutan">Paro</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Paro_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Paro Valley">Paro Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CS1_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CS1-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
