           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><b><a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a></b></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_10x118" style="position:absolute; left:10px; top:118px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><b><a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a></b></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_120x123" style="position:absolute; left:120px; top:123px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><b><a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a></b></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_53x113" style="position:absolute; left:53px; top:113px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Lepcha_language" title="Lepcha language">Lepcha</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_58x126" style="position:absolute; left:58px; top:126px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Lhokpu_language" title="Lhokpu language">Lhokpu</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_165x111" style="position:absolute; left:165px; top:111px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Kheng_language" title="Kheng language">Kheng</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_192x119" style="position:absolute; left:192px; top:119px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><a href="/wiki/Gongduk_language" title="Gongduk language">Gongduk</a></small></span>
          </div> 
          <div id="annotation_228x100" style="position:absolute; left:228px; top:100px; line-height:110%">
           <span style="background-color:transparent;"><small><b><a href="/wiki/Tshangla_language" title="Tshangla language">Tshangla</a><br><a href="/wiki/Tshangla_language" title="Tshangla language">(Sharchopkha)</a></b></small></span>
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div style="visibility:hidden">
          <div class="noresize">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_Bhutan_with_labels.svg" title="File:Languages of Bhutan with labels.svg"><img alt="Languages of Bhutan.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Languages_of_Bhutan.svg/350px-Languages_of_Bhutan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Languages_of_Bhutan.svg/525px-Languages_of_Bhutan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Languages_of_Bhutan.svg/700px-Languages_of_Bhutan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="875" data-file-height="476"></a>
          </div>
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Bhutan" title="Languages of Bhutan">Languages of Bhutan</a>
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The national language is <a href="/wiki/Dzongkha" title="Dzongkha">Dzongkha</a> (Bhutanese), one of 53 languages in the <a href="/wiki/Tibetic_languages" title="Tibetic languages">Tibetan language</a> family. The script, locally called <i>Chhokey</i> (literally, "Dharma language"), is identical to classical Tibetan. In Bhutan's education system, English is the medium of instruction, while Dzongkha is taught as the national language. <i><a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">Ethnologue</a></i> lists 24 languages currently spoken in Bhutan, all of them in the <a href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman" class="mw-redirect" title="Tibeto-Burman">Tibeto-Burman</a> family, except <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIDCM_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIDCM-114">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Until the 1980s, the government sponsored the teaching of Nepali in schools in southern Bhutan. With the adoption of the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Driglam_Namzhag&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Driglam Namzhag (page does not exist)">Driglam Namzhag</a></i> (Bhutanese code of etiquette) and its expansion into the idea of strengthening the role of Dzongkha, Nepali was dropped from the curriculum. The languages of Bhutan are still not well characterized, and several have yet to be recorded in an in-depth academic grammar. Before the 1980s, the <a href="/wiki/Lhotshampa" title="Lhotshampa">Lhotshampa</a> (Nepali-speaking community), mainly based in southern Bhutan, constituted approximately 30% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-CIDCM_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIDCM-114">[114]</a></sup> However, after a purge of Lhotshaampas from 1990 to 1992 this number might not accurately reflect the current population. </p>
      <p>Dzongkha is partially intelligible with <a href="/wiki/Sikkimese_language" title="Sikkimese language">Sikkimese</a> and spoken natively by 25% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Tshangla_language" title="Tshangla language">Tshangla</a>, the language of the Sharchop and the principal pre-Tibetan language of Bhutan, is spoken by a greater number of people. It is not easily classified and may constitute an independent branch of Tibeto-Burman. <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a> speakers constituted some 40% of the population as of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. The larger minority languages are <a href="/wiki/Dzala_language" title="Dzala language">Dzala</a> (11%), <a href="/wiki/Limbu_language" title="Limbu language">Limbu</a> (10%), <a href="/wiki/Kheng_language" title="Kheng language">Kheng</a> (8%), and <a href="/wiki/Bantawa_language" title="Bantawa language">Rai</a> (8%). There are no reliable sources for the ethnic or linguistic composition of Bhutan, so these numbers do not add up to 100%. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Bhutan" title="Health in Bhutan">Health in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan has a <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> of 70.2 years (69.9 for males and 70.5 for females) according to the latest data for 2016 from the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Basic healthcare in Bhutan is free, as provided by the Constitution of Bhutan.<sup id="cite_ref-CoBE_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CoBE-192">[191]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bhutan" title="Education in Bhutan">Education in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ILCS_Campus_Tagse_Bhutan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/ILCS_Campus_Tagse_Bhutan.jpg/220px-ILCS_Campus_Tagse_Bhutan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/ILCS_Campus_Tagse_Bhutan.jpg/330px-ILCS_Campus_Tagse_Bhutan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/ILCS_Campus_Tagse_Bhutan.jpg/440px-ILCS_Campus_Tagse_Bhutan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ILCS_Campus_Tagse_Bhutan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The ILCS Campus Taktse Bhutan.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Historically, education in Bhutan was <a href="/wiki/Monasticism" title="Monasticism">monastic</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Secularity" title="Secularity">secular</a> school education for the general population introduced in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-193">[192]</a></sup> The mountainous landscape poses barriers to integrated educational services.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-193">[192]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Today, Bhutan has two decentralized universities with eleven constituent colleges spread across the kingdom. These are the <a href="/wiki/Royal_University_of_Bhutan" title="Royal University of Bhutan">Royal University of Bhutan</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Khesar_Gyalpo_University_of_Medical_Sciences&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Khesar Gyalpo University of Medical Sciences (page does not exist)">Khesar Gyalpo University of Medical Sciences</a>, respectively. The first <a href="/wiki/Five-Year_Plans_of_Bhutan" title="Five-Year Plans of Bhutan">five-year plan</a> provided for a central education authority—in the form of a director of education appointed in 1961—and an organized, modern school system with free and universal primary education. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Education_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Education program">Education programs</a> were given a boost in 1990, when the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> (see Glossary) granted a US$7.13&nbsp;million loan for staff training and development, specialist services, equipment and furniture purchases, salaries and other recurrent costs, and facility rehabilitation and construction at <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bhutan_Polytechnic" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Bhutan Polytechnic">Royal Bhutan Polytechnic</a>. </p>
      <p>Since the beginning of modern education in Bhutan, teachers from India—especially <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>—have served in some of the most remote villages of Bhutan. Thus, 43 retired teachers who had served for the longest length of time were personally invited to <a href="/wiki/Thimphu" title="Thimphu">Thimphu</a>, Bhutan during the Teachers' Day celebrations in 2018, where they were honored and individually thanked by His Majesty <a href="/wiki/Jigme_Khesar_Namgyel_Wangchuck" title="Jigme Khesar Namgyel Wangchuck">Jigme Khesar Namgyel Wangchuck</a>. To celebrate 50 years of diplomatic relations between Bhutan and India, Bhutan's Education Minister, <a href="/wiki/Jai_Bir_Rai" title="Jai Bir Rai">Jai Bir Rai</a> honored 80 retired teachers who served in Bhutan at a special ceremony organized at <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> on 6 January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> Currently, there are 121 teachers from India placed in schools across Bhutan. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bhutan" title="Culture of Bhutan">Culture of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutanese_thanka_of_Mt._Meru_and_the_Buddhist_Universe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bhutanese_thanka_of_Mt._Meru_and_the_Buddhist_Universe.jpg/170px-Bhutanese_thanka_of_Mt._Meru_and_the_Buddhist_Universe.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bhutanese_thanka_of_Mt._Meru_and_the_Buddhist_Universe.jpg/255px-Bhutanese_thanka_of_Mt._Meru_and_the_Buddhist_Universe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bhutanese_thanka_of_Mt._Meru_and_the_Buddhist_Universe.jpg/340px-Bhutanese_thanka_of_Mt._Meru_and_the_Buddhist_Universe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1558" data-file-height="2250"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutanese_thanka_of_Mt._Meru_and_the_Buddhist_Universe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bhutanese <i><a href="/wiki/Thanka" class="mw-redirect" title="Thanka">thanka</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Meru_(mythology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Meru (mythology)">Mt. Meru</a> and the Buddhist universe (19th century, <a href="/wiki/Trongsa" title="Trongsa">Trongsa Dzong</a>, Trongsa, Bhutan)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan has a rich and unique cultural heritage that has largely remained intact because of its isolation from the rest of the world until the mid-20th century. One of the main attractions for tourists is the country's culture and traditions. Bhutanese tradition is deeply steeped in its Buddhist heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is the second most dominant religion in Bhutan, being most prevalent in the southern regions.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> The government is increasingly making efforts to preserve and sustain the current culture and traditions of the country. Because of its largely unspoiled natural environment and cultural heritage, Bhutan has been referred to as <i>The Last <a href="/wiki/Shangri-La" title="Shangri-La">Shangri-La</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While Bhutanese citizens are free to travel abroad, Bhutan is viewed as inaccessible by many foreigners. Another reason for it being an unpopular destination is the cost, which is high for tourists on tighter budgets. Entry is free for citizens of India, Bangladesh, and the Maldives, but all other foreigners are required to sign up with a Bhutanese tour operator and pay around US$250 per day that they stay in the country, though this fee covers most travel, lodging and meal expenses.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> Bhutan received 37,482 visitor arrivals in 2011, of which 25% were for meetings, incentives, conferencing, and exhibitions.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bhutan is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_smoking_bans#Bhutan" title="List of smoking bans">first nation in the world</a> to ban <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>. It has been illegal to smoke in public or sell tobacco, according to <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Control_Act_of_Bhutan_2010" title="Tobacco Control Act of Bhutan 2010">Tobacco Control Act of Bhutan 2010</a>. Violators are fined the equivalent of $232—a month's salary in Bhutan.<sup id="cite_ref-LP_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LP-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dress">Dress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Dress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The national dress for Bhutanese men is the <i><a href="/wiki/Gho" title="Gho">gho</a></i>, a knee-length robe tied at the waist by a cloth belt known as the <i>kera</i>. Women wear an ankle-length dress, the <i><a href="/wiki/Kira_(dress)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kira (dress)">kira</a></i>, which is clipped at the shoulders with two identical brooches called the <i>koma</i> and tied at the waist with kera. An accompaniment to the kira is a long-sleeved blouse, the "<i>wonju</i>," which is worn underneath the kira. A long-sleeved, jacket-like garment called the "<i>toego</i>" is worn over the kira. The sleeves of the wonju and the tego are folded together at the cuffs, inside out. Social status and class determine the textures, colors, and decorations that embellish the garments. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Jewelry" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewelry">Jewelry</a> is commonly worn by women, especially during religious festivals ("<a href="/wiki/Tsechu" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsechu">tsechus</a>") and public gatherings. To strengthen Bhutan's identity as an independent country, Bhutanese law requires all Bhutanese government employees to wear the national dress at work and all citizens to wear the national dress while visiting schools and other government offices though many citizens, particularly adults, choose to wear the customary dress as formal attire. </p>
      <p>Varicolored scarves, known as <i>rachu</i> for women and <i><a href="/wiki/Kabney" title="Kabney">kabney</a></i> for men, are important indicators of social standing, as Bhutan has traditionally been a <a href="/wiki/Feudal" class="mw-redirect" title="Feudal">feudal</a> society; in particular, red is the most common color worn by women. The "Bura Maap" (Red Scarf) is one of highest honors a Bhutanese civilian can receive. It, as well as the title of <a href="/wiki/Dasho" title="Dasho">Dasho</a>, comes from the throne in recognition of an individual's outstanding service to the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> On previous occasions, the King himself conferred Bura Maaps to outstanding individuals such as the Director General of Department Hydropower and Power System, Yeshi Wangdi, the Deputy Chairperson of National Council, Dasho Dr. Sonam Kinga, and former National Assembly Speaker, Dasho Ugyen Dorji.<sup id="cite_ref-MyUser_Bbs.bt_October_15_2020c_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MyUser_Bbs.bt_October_15_2020c-202">[201]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:National_Library-Thimphu-Bhutan-2008_01_23.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/National_Library-Thimphu-Bhutan-2008_01_23.jpg/220px-National_Library-Thimphu-Bhutan-2008_01_23.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/National_Library-Thimphu-Bhutan-2008_01_23.jpg/330px-National_Library-Thimphu-Bhutan-2008_01_23.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/National_Library-Thimphu-Bhutan-2008_01_23.jpg/440px-National_Library-Thimphu-Bhutan-2008_01_23.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2136"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:National_Library-Thimphu-Bhutan-2008_01_23.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The National Library of Bhutan during snowfall
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Bhutan" title="Architecture of Bhutan">Architecture of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhutanese architecture">Bhutanese architecture</a> remains distinctively traditional, employing <a href="/wiki/Rammed_earth" title="Rammed earth">rammed earth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wattle_and_daub" title="Wattle and daub">wattle and daub</a> construction methods, stone masonry, and intricate woodwork around windows and roofs. Traditional architecture uses no nails or iron bars in construction.<sup id="cite_ref-LP_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LP-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc98_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc98-204">[203]</a></sup> Characteristic of the region is a type of castle fortress known as the <a href="/wiki/Dzong_architecture" title="Dzong architecture">dzong</a>. Since ancient times, the dzongs have served as the religious and secular <a href="/wiki/Administrative_center" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative center">administrative centers</a> for their respective districts.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_El_Paso" title="University of Texas at El Paso">University of Texas at El Paso</a> in the United States has adopted Bhutanese architecture for its buildings on campus, as have the nearby Hilton Garden Inn and other buildings in the city of El Paso.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">Public holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Public holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Bhutan has <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Bhutan" title="Public holidays in Bhutan">numerous public holidays</a>, most of which coincide with traditional, seasonal, secular or religious festivals. They include the winter solstice (around 1 January, depending on the <a href="/wiki/Lunar_calendar" title="Lunar calendar">lunar calendar</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> Lunar New Year (February or March),<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> the King's birthday and the anniversary of his coronation, the official end of <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> season (22 September),<sup id="cite_ref-RCSC_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCSC-209">[208]</a></sup> National Day (17 December),<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> and various <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> celebrations. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_industry">Film industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Film industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Bhutan" title="Cinema of Bhutan">Cinema of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan-masked-dance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Bhutan-masked-dance.jpg/170px-Bhutan-masked-dance.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Bhutan-masked-dance.jpg/255px-Bhutan-masked-dance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Bhutan-masked-dance.jpg/340px-Bhutan-masked-dance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="987"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan-masked-dance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Chaam</i>, sacred masked dances, are annually performed during religious festivals.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bhutan" title="Music of Bhutan">Music of Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Dance dramas and masked dances such as the <a href="/wiki/Cham_dance" title="Cham dance">Cham dance</a> are common traditional features at festivals, usually accompanied by traditional music. At these events, dancers depict heroes, demons, <a href="/wiki/Daemon_(classical_mythology)" title="Daemon (classical mythology)">dæmons</a>, death heads, animals, gods, and caricatures of common people by wearing colorful wooden or composition face masks and stylized costumes. The dancers enjoy royal patronage, and preserve ancient folk and religious customs and perpetuate the ancient lore and art of mask-making. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bhutan" title="Music of Bhutan">music of Bhutan</a> can generally be divided into traditional and modern varieties; traditional music comprises religious and folk genres, the latter including <i><a href="/wiki/Zhungdra" title="Zhungdra">zhungdra</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Boedra" title="Boedra">boedra</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Greenwood_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenwood-211">[210]</a></sup> The modern <i><a href="/wiki/Rigsar" title="Rigsar">rigsar</a></i> is played on a mix of traditional instruments and electronic keyboards, and dates back to the early 1990s; it shows the influence of Indian popular music, a hybrid form of traditional and Western popular influences.<sup id="cite_ref-k1_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-k1-212">[211]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_structure">Family structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Family structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Bhutanese families, inheritance generally passes <a href="/wiki/Matrilineally" class="mw-redirect" title="Matrilineally">matrilineally</a> through the female rather than the male line. Daughters will inherit their parents' house. A man is expected to make his own way in the world and often moves to his wife's home. <a href="/wiki/Love_marriage" title="Love marriage">Love marriages</a> are more common in urban areas, but the tradition of <a href="/wiki/Arranged_marriage" title="Arranged marriage">arranged marriages</a> among acquainted families is still prevalent in most of the rural areas. Although uncommon, <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamy</a> is accepted, often being a device to keep property in a contained family unit rather than dispersing it.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> The previous king, <a href="/wiki/Jigme_Singye_Wangchuck" title="Jigme Singye Wangchuck">Jigme Singye Wangchuck</a>, who abdicated in 2006, had four queens, all of whom are sisters. The current king, <a href="/wiki/Jigme_Khesar_Namgyel_Wangchuck" title="Jigme Khesar Namgyel Wangchuck">Jigme Khesar Namgyel Wangchuck</a>, wed <a href="/wiki/Jetsun_Pema_(born_1990)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jetsun Pema (born 1990)">Jetsun Pema</a>, then 21, a commoner and daughter of a pilot, on 13 October 2011. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_cuisine" title="Bhutanese cuisine">Bhutanese cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutanese_red_rice_with_chicken_and_spinach.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bhutanese_red_rice_with_chicken_and_spinach.jpg/220px-Bhutanese_red_rice_with_chicken_and_spinach.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bhutanese_red_rice_with_chicken_and_spinach.jpg/330px-Bhutanese_red_rice_with_chicken_and_spinach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bhutanese_red_rice_with_chicken_and_spinach.jpg/440px-Bhutanese_red_rice_with_chicken_and_spinach.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="798"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutanese_red_rice_with_chicken_and_spinach.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional dish with lemon glazed chicken, sauteed spinach and steamed Bhutanese red rice
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">Rice</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_red_rice" title="Bhutanese red rice">red rice</a>), <a href="/wiki/Buckwheat" title="Buckwheat">buckwheat</a>, and increasingly <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, are the staples of <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_cuisine" title="Bhutanese cuisine">Bhutanese cuisine</a>. The local diet also includes pork, beef, <a href="/wiki/Yak" class="mw-redirect" title="Yak">yak</a> meat, chicken, and lamb. Soups and stews of meat and dried vegetables spiced with chilies and cheese are prepared. <i><a href="/wiki/Ema_datshi" title="Ema datshi">Ema datshi</a></i>, made very spicy with cheese and chilies, might be called the national dish for its ubiquity and the pride that Bhutanese have for it. Dairy foods, particularly butter and cheese from yaks and cows, are also popular, and indeed almost all milk is turned into butter and cheese. Popular beverages include <a href="/wiki/Butter_tea" title="Butter tea">butter tea</a>, black tea, locally brewed <i><a href="/wiki/Ara_(drink)" title="Ara (drink)">ara</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Rice_wine" title="Rice wine">rice wine</a>), and beer.<sup id="cite_ref-LP_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LP-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Bhutan" title="Sports in Bhutan">Sports in Bhutan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_archery.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Bhutan_archery.jpg/300px-Bhutan_archery.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Bhutan_archery.jpg/450px-Bhutan_archery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Bhutan_archery.jpg/600px-Bhutan_archery.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1072" data-file-height="720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bhutan_archery.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Changlimithang_Stadium" title="Changlimithang Stadium">Changlimithang Stadium</a> during a parade.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Taekwondo_YOG_2018_Girls_49kg_BHU-VIE_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Taekwondo_YOG_2018_Girls_49kg_BHU-VIE_05.jpg/220px-Taekwondo_YOG_2018_Girls_49kg_BHU-VIE_05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Taekwondo_YOG_2018_Girls_49kg_BHU-VIE_05.jpg/330px-Taekwondo_YOG_2018_Girls_49kg_BHU-VIE_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Taekwondo_YOG_2018_Girls_49kg_BHU-VIE_05.jpg/440px-Taekwondo_YOG_2018_Girls_49kg_BHU-VIE_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Taekwondo_YOG_2018_Girls_49kg_BHU-VIE_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">Taekwondo</a> between Bhutan and Vietnam
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bhutan's national and most popular sport is <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">archery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-impress_BHUTAN_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impress_BHUTAN-215">[214]</a></sup> Competitions are held regularly in most villages. It differs from <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> standards in technical details such as the placement of the targets and atmosphere. Two targets are placed over 100 meters (330&nbsp;ft) apart, and teams shoot from one end of the field to the other. Each member of the team shoots two arrows per round. Traditional Bhutanese archery is a social event, and competitions are organized between villages, towns, and amateur teams. There is usually plenty of food and drink complete with singing and dancing. Attempts to distract an opponent include standing around the target and making fun of the shooter's ability. <a href="/wiki/Darts" title="Darts">Darts</a> (<i>khuru</i>) is an equally popular outdoor team sport, in which heavy wooden darts pointed with a 10&nbsp;cm nail are thrown at a paperback-sized target 10 to 20 meters (33 to 66&nbsp;ft) away. </p>
      <p>Another traditional sport is the <i><a href="/wiki/Digor_(sports)" title="Digor (sports)">Digor</a></i>, which resembles the <a href="/wiki/Shot_put" title="Shot put">shot put</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horseshoes" title="Horseshoes">horseshoe throwing</a>. </p>
      <p>Another popular sport is <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-impress_BHUTAN_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impress_BHUTAN-215">[214]</a></sup> In 2002, Bhutan's <a href="/wiki/Bhutan_national_football_team" title="Bhutan national football team">national football team</a> played <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_national_football_team" title="Montserrat national football team">Montserrat</a>, in what was billed as <a href="/wiki/The_Other_Final" title="The Other Final">The Other Final</a>; the match took place on the same day Brazil played Germany in the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2002 FIFA World Cup Final">World Cup final</a>, but at the time Bhutan and Montserrat were the world's two lowest ranked teams. The match was held in Thimphu's <a href="/wiki/Changlimithang_Stadium" title="Changlimithang Stadium">Changlimithang National Stadium</a>, and Bhutan won 4–0. A documentary of the match was made by the Dutch filmmaker Johan Kramer. Bhutan won its first two FIFA World Cup Qualifying matches, beating <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_football_team" title="Sri Lanka national football team">Sri Lanka</a> 1–0 in Sri Lanka and 2–1 in Bhutan, taking the aggregate at 3–1.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> has also gained popularity in Bhutan, particularly since the introduction of television channels from India. The <a href="/wiki/Bhutan_national_cricket_team" title="Bhutan national cricket team">Bhutan national cricket team</a> is one of the most successful affiliate nations in the region. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women_in_the_workforce">Women in the workforce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Women in the workforce">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Women have begun to participate more in the work force and their participation is one of the highest in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-:13_108-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-108">[108]</a></sup> However, the unemployment rates among women are still higher than those of men and women are in more unsecure work fields, such as agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-217">[216]</a></sup> Most of the work that women do outside of the home is in family-based agriculture which is insecure and is one of the reasons why women are falling behind men when it comes to income.<sup id="cite_ref-:13_108-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-108">[108]</a></sup> Women also, in general, work lower-quality jobs than men and only earn 75% of men's earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-218">[217]</a></sup> The unemployment rate among women is also higher than that of men.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-217">[216]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women_in_the_household">Women in the household</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Women in the household">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Rooted deep in Bhutan culture is the idea of selflessness and the women of Bhutan take on this role in the context of the household.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> Bhutan culture has shown a tolerance for domestic violence with nearly 1/4 of all women having had experienced some form of violence from their husband or partner.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_217-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-217">[216]</a></sup> Some Bhutanese communities have what is referred to as matrilineal communities, where the eldest daughter receives the largest share of the land.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-218">[217]</a></sup> This is due to the belief that she will stay and take care of her parents while the son will move out and work to get his own land and for his own family.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_218-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-218">[217]</a></sup> Importantly, land ownership does not necessarily equate to economic benefits - despite the eldest daughter having control of the house, it is the husband that is in charge of making decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_218-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-218">[217]</a></sup> However, the younger generation has stepped away from this belief, in splitting the land evenly between the children instead of the eldest daughter inheriting the most land.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_218-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-218">[217]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Women.27s_health"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women's_health">Women's health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Women's health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Throughout Bhutan, there has been an improvement in reproductive health services that has led to a drastic drop in maternal mortality rate, dropping from 1,000 in 1990 to 180 in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_218-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-218">[217]</a></sup> There has also been an increase in contraceptive use from less than 1/3 in 2003 to 2/3 in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_218-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-218">[217]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhutan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
